* Senior club appearances and goals counted for the domestic league only</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Stephen Roger Bruce</b> (born 31 December 1960) is an English professional <a href="/wiki/Manager_(association_football)" title="Manager (association football)">football manager</a> and former <a href="/wiki/Football_player" title="Football player">player</a> who played as a <a href="/wiki/Centre-back" class="mw-redirect" title="Centre-back">centre-back</a>. He is the current manager of <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>.
</p><p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Corbridge" title="Corbridge">Corbridge</a>, Northumberland, he was a promising schoolboy footballer but was rejected by several professional clubs. He was on the verge of quitting the game altogether when he was offered a trial with <a href="/wiki/Gillingham_F.C." title="Gillingham F.C.">Gillingham</a>. Bruce was offered an apprenticeship and went on to play more than 200&#160;games for the club before joining <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a> in 1984, winning the <a href="/wiki/1985_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="1985 Football League Cup Final">League Cup in 1985</a>. In 1987, he moved to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>, with whom he achieved great success, winning twelve trophies including three <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> titles, three <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cups</a>, one <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="European Cup Winners&#39; Cup">European Cup Winners' Cup</a>.  He also became the first English player of the 20th century to captain a team to <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">the Double</a>. Despite his success on the field, he was never selected to play for the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national team</a>. Commentators and contemporaries have described him as one of the best English players of the 1980s and 1990s never to play for his country at full international level.
</p><p>Bruce began his managerial career with <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a>, and spent short periods of time managing <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a> before joining <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a> in 2001. He twice led Birmingham to <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">promotion</a> to the Premier League during his tenure of nearly six years, but resigned in 2007 to begin a second spell as manager of Wigan. At the end of the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_in_English_football" title="2008–09 in English football">2008–09 season</a> he resigned to take over as manager of <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>, a post he held until he was dismissed in November 2011. Seven months later, he was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a> and led the club to two promotions to the Premier League, as well as the <a href="/wiki/2014_FA_Cup_Final" title="2014 FA Cup Final">2014 FA Cup Final</a>, before leaving in July 2016. He took over at <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> four months later but was dismissed in October 2018. He took over as manager of Sheffield Wednesday in February 2019 and left in July that year to take over at Newcastle United. <sup id="cite_ref-newcastle-appoint_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newcastle-appoint-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Corbridge_uk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Corbridge_uk.jpg/220px-Corbridge_uk.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Corbridge_uk.jpg/330px-Corbridge_uk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Corbridge_uk.jpg/440px-Corbridge_uk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="766" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Corbridge_uk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Corbridge" title="Corbridge">Corbridge</a>, Bruce's place of birth</div></div></div>
<p>Bruce was born in <a href="/wiki/Corbridge" title="Corbridge">Corbridge</a> in Northumberland, the elder of two sons of Joe and Sheenagh Bruce.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> His father was local, and his mother had been born in <a href="/wiki/Bangor,_County_Down" title="Bangor, County Down">Bangor</a> in Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-Ireland_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ireland-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vital_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vital-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The family lived in Daisy Hill near <a href="/wiki/Wallsend" title="Wallsend">Wallsend</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and Bruce attended <a href="/wiki/Benfield_School" title="Benfield School">Benfield School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SB38_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB38-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bruce, a boyhood fan of <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>, said that he sneaked into <a href="/wiki/St_James%27_Park" title="St James&#39; Park">St James' Park</a> without paying to watch the team play, saying "I have always been a <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a> lad and when I was a kid, I crawled under the turnstiles to get in to try and save a <a href="/wiki/Shilling" title="Shilling">bob</a> or whatever it was. They were my team, I went to support them as a boy and being a <a href="/wiki/Geordie" title="Geordie">Geordie</a> it's in-bred, you follow the club still the same today."<sup id="cite_ref-ManU_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ManU-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Like several other future professionals from the area,<sup id="cite_ref-MULeg_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MULeg-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> he played football for <a href="/wiki/Wallsend_Boys_Club" title="Wallsend Boys Club">Wallsend Boys Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ManU_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ManU-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He was also selected for the Newcastle Schools representative team, and at the age of 13 was among a group of players from the team selected to serve as <a href="/wiki/Ball_boy" title="Ball boy">ball boys</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1974_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="1974 Football League Cup Final">1974 League Cup Final</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SB74_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB74-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Having been turned down by several professional clubs, including Newcastle United, <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C." title="Derby County F.C.">Derby County</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southport_F.C." title="Southport F.C.">Southport</a>, Bruce was about to start work as an apprentice plumber at the <a href="/wiki/Swan_Hunter" title="Swan Hunter">Swan Hunter</a> dockyard when he was offered a trial by <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Third Division</a> club <a href="/wiki/Gillingham_F.C." title="Gillingham F.C.">Gillingham</a>, whose manager <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Summers" title="Gerry Summers">Gerry Summers</a> had seen him playing for Wallsend in an international youth tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-SB39_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB39-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He travelled down to <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a> with another player from the Wallsend club, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Beardsley" title="Peter Beardsley">Peter Beardsley</a>, but although Gillingham signed Bruce as an apprentice, they turned Beardsley away.<sup id="cite_ref-Buster2_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buster2-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> At the time Bruce was playing as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a>, but he was switched to the centre of defence by the head of Gillingham's youth scheme, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Collins_(footballer,_born_1920)" title="Bill Collins (footballer, born 1920)">Bill Collins</a>, whom Bruce cites as the single biggest influence on his career.<sup id="cite_ref-Buster2_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buster2-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Buster_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buster-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_career">Playing career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gillingham">Gillingham</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Priestfield1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Priestfield1.jpg/220px-Priestfield1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Priestfield1.jpg/330px-Priestfield1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Priestfield1.jpg/440px-Priestfield1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="691" data-file-height="470" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Priestfield1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Priestfield_Stadium" title="Priestfield Stadium">Priestfield Stadium</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/Gillingham_F.C." title="Gillingham F.C.">Gillingham</a>, where Bruce began his playing career</div></div></div>
<p>Bruce spent the <a href="/wiki/1978%E2%80%9379_in_English_football" title="1978–79 in English football">1978–79 season</a> in Gillingham's <a href="/wiki/Reserve_team" title="Reserve team">reserve team</a> and, despite playing in defence, scored 18&#160;goals to finish the season as top scorer.<sup id="cite_ref-triggs_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triggs-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In January 1979, he was selected to represent the <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-18_football_team" title="England national under-18 football team">England youth</a> team, and he went on to gain eight caps, participating in the <a href="/wiki/1980_UEFA_European_Under-18_Championship" title="1980 UEFA European Under-18 Championship">1980 UEFA European Under-18 Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SB52_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB52-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> He came close to making his debut for the club's senior team in May 1979, but Summers decided at the last minute that, as Gillingham were chasing <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">promotion</a> from the Third Division, Bruce was not yet ready to handle the pressure of the occasion.<sup id="cite_ref-SB53_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB53-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> He eventually made his senior debut in a <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a> tie against <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town</a> on 11 August 1979,<sup id="cite_ref-First_season_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-First_season-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and made an immediate impact in the team, winning the club's Player of the Year award at the end of the <a href="/wiki/1979%E2%80%9380_in_English_football" title="1979–80 in English football">1979–80 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SB57_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB57-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> He went on to make more than 200&#160;appearances for the club,<sup id="cite_ref-triggs_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triggs-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and was twice voted into the <a href="/wiki/Professional_Footballers%27_Association" title="Professional Footballers&#39; Association">Professional Footballers' Association</a>'s Third Division Team of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-triggs352_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triggs352-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Confident that he was being targeted by clubs from higher divisions, Bruce resolved not to sign a new contract with Gillingham when his existing deal expired at the end of the <a href="/wiki/1983%E2%80%9384_in_English_football" title="1983–84 in English football">1983–84 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SB60_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB60-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In an April 1983 match against <a href="/wiki/Newport_County_A.F.C." title="Newport County A.F.C.">Newport County</a>, he attempted, in a moment of anger, to deliberately injure opposition player <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Tynan" title="Tommy Tynan">Tommy Tynan</a>, but connected awkwardly and succeeded only in breaking his own leg, leaving him unable to play again for six months.<sup id="cite_ref-SB62_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB62-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He returned in time to play a key role in Gillingham achieving two draws against <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> in 1984, attracting the attention once again of <a href="/wiki/Scout_(sport)" title="Scout (sport)">scouts</a> from <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a> clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-Buster2_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buster2-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Cox_(footballer)" title="Arthur Cox (footballer)">Arthur Cox</a>, manager of Bruce's beloved Newcastle United, expressed an interest in signing the player, but resigned from his job before any further action could be taken.<sup id="cite_ref-SB65_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB65-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Bruce eventually opted to sign for <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a> in August 1984 for a fee variously reported as £125,000<sup id="cite_ref-sang_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sang-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> or £135,000.<sup id="cite_ref-triggs_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triggs-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, he was voted into Gillingham's <a href="/wiki/Gillingham_F.C._Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Gillingham F.C. Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GFCHOFR_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GFCHOFR-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norwich_City">Norwich City</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SteveBruceNorwich1980s.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/SteveBruceNorwich1980s.JPG/170px-SteveBruceNorwich1980s.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/SteveBruceNorwich1980s.JPG/255px-SteveBruceNorwich1980s.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/SteveBruceNorwich1980s.JPG/340px-SteveBruceNorwich1980s.JPG 2x" data-file-width="427" data-file-height="613" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SteveBruceNorwich1980s.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bruce pictured circa 1986, during his time with <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a></div></div></div>
<p>Bruce began the <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_in_English_football" title="1984–85 in English football">1984–85 season</a> by scoring an <a href="/wiki/Own_goal" title="Own goal">own goal</a> in the first minute of his debut for Norwich against <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> but went on to score the team's winning goal in the semi-final of the League Cup against local rivals <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_Town_F.C." title="Ipswich Town F.C.">Ipswich Town</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and was named man of the match in Norwich's victory in <a href="/wiki/1985_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="1985 Football League Cup Final">the final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LC85_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LC85-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Bruce was voted <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_Player_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwich City Player of the Year">Norwich City Player of the Year</a>, but the team was <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">relegated</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ash_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ash-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Bruce played in every match as Norwich won promotion back to the top division at the first time of asking in the <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_in_English_football" title="1985–86 in English football">1985–86 season</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ash_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ash-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2D_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2D-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> after which he was chosen to replace the departing <a href="/wiki/Dave_Watson" title="Dave Watson">Dave Watson</a> as club <a href="/wiki/Captain_(sports)" title="Captain (sports)">captain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SB85_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB85-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The following season he helped the club to its highest ever league finish of fifth position.<sup id="cite_ref-8695history_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8695history-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1987, he was chosen to captain the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_B_team" title="England national football B team">England B team</a> in a match against the <a href="/wiki/Malta_national_football_team" title="Malta national football team">full national team of Malta</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-SB88_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB88-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> but it was to be his only appearance in an England shirt, and he has subsequently been described as one of the best defenders of his era never to be selected for <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">the full England team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MattU_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MattU-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fi_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fi-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Bruce later stated, "I bumped into former England manager <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Robson" title="Bobby Robson">Bobby Robson</a> in <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">Benfica</a><i> (sic)</i>. He came up to me and said 'I should have capped you'. It was nice to hear but it still didn't get me one .... I'll always be a little disappointed I didn't get one."<sup id="cite_ref-champs_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-champs-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bruce began to attract the attention of big-name clubs in late 1987, with <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a> all reported to be interested in signing him.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Manchester United quickly emerged as the front runners for his signature, and Bruce publicly expressed his desire to sign for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The deal came close to collapsing when Norwich asked for a transfer fee of £900,000 after initially agreeing to accept £800,000,<sup id="cite_ref-gone_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gone-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> leading to Bruce refusing to play any further matches for the club, which he felt was jeopardising his dream move.<sup id="cite_ref-SB93_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB93-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> On 17 December 1987, shortly before his 27th birthday, the deal was concluded and Bruce officially left <a href="/wiki/Carrow_Road" title="Carrow Road">Carrow Road</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-gone_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gone-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> for a fee reported as £800,000<sup id="cite_ref-sang_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sang-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> or £825,000.<sup id="cite_ref-MULeg_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MULeg-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Norwich fans remembered his contribution, and in 2002 voted him into the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Norwich_City_F.C._Hall_of_Fame_members" title="List of Norwich City F.C. Hall of Fame members">Norwich City Hall of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_United">Manchester United</span></h3>
<p>Bruce made his Manchester United debut in a 2–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> on 19 December 1987,<sup id="cite_ref-all_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-all-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and played in 21 of United's remaining 22&#160;league fixtures,<sup id="cite_ref-all2_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-all2-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> helping the club to a top two place in the First Division for the first time since 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-FCHDMU_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHDMU-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The team only finished in mid-table in the following season,<sup id="cite_ref-FCHDMU2_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCHDMU2-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> prompting manager <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Alex Ferguson</a> to bring in several new players, including <a href="/wiki/Gary_Pallister" title="Gary Pallister">Gary Pallister</a>, who joined the club in August 1989 from <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IP2_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IP2-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> His partnership with Bruce in the centre of defence was described in 2006 by the then-United captain, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Neville" title="Gary Neville">Gary Neville</a>, as the best in the club's history.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> "Dolly and Daisy", as the pair were affectionately known, are described as "arguably the best" on the official Manchester United website.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Bruce and Pallister were part of the team that won the <a href="/wiki/1990_FA_Cup_Final" title="1990 FA Cup Final">1990 FA Cup Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a> in a replay.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the lifting of the five-year ban on English clubs from European competitions, which had been imposed after the <a href="/wiki/Heysel_Stadium_disaster" title="Heysel Stadium disaster">Heysel Stadium disaster</a>, United became England's first entrants into the <a href="/wiki/European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="European Cup Winners&#39; Cup">European Cup Winners' Cup</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1990–91 European Cup Winners&#39; Cup">1990–91 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Bruce played regularly, and scored three goals, in the team's progress to <a href="/wiki/1991_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup_Final" title="1991 European Cup Winners&#39; Cup Final">the final</a> against <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-stret91_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stret91-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> He came close to scoring the first goal, only for <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hughes" title="Mark Hughes">Mark Hughes</a> to deflect the ball over the line and claim the goal,<sup id="cite_ref-CWC_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CWC-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> and United went on to win the game 2–1. This was a particularly high-scoring season for Bruce, who found the net 13&#160;times in the First Division and 19&#160;times in total in all competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-stret91_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stret91-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> He also played again at Wembley, in the <a href="/wiki/1991_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="1991 Football League Cup Final">League Cup final</a>, in which United were defeated by <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a> of the Second Division.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steve_Bruce_at_the_cliff_-march_92.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Steve_Bruce_at_the_cliff_-march_92.JPG/170px-Steve_Bruce_at_the_cliff_-march_92.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Steve_Bruce_at_the_cliff_-march_92.JPG/255px-Steve_Bruce_at_the_cliff_-march_92.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/Steve_Bruce_at_the_cliff_-march_92.JPG 2x" data-file-width="310" data-file-height="452" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steve_Bruce_at_the_cliff_-march_92.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bruce pictured in 1992, during his time at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a></div></div></div>
<p>Bruce missed several weeks of the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_in_English_football" title="1991–92 in English football">1991–92 season</a> when he underwent an operation on a longstanding <a href="/wiki/Hernia" title="Hernia">hernia</a> problem,<sup id="cite_ref-recovery_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recovery-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> in which <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a>, after a season-long tussle, beat Manchester United to the championship by four points.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Bruce helped United win their first-ever League Cup in April 1992,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> captaining the team in <a href="/wiki/1992_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="1992 Football League Cup Final">the final</a> in place of the injured <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Robson" title="Bryan Robson">Bryan Robson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Injuries continued to take their toll upon Robson during the <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_in_English_football" title="1992–93 in English football">1992–93 season</a>, leading to Bruce captaining the team in the majority of United's matches during the first season of the new <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-champs_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-champs-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Bruce scored two late goals in a win over Sheffield Wednesday which proved decisive in United winning the inaugural Premier League title,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> the first time the club had won the championship of English football since 1967, and he and Robson received the trophy jointly after the home victory over <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> on 3 May.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the height of his success with United, Bruce was contacted by <a href="/wiki/Jack_Charlton" title="Jack Charlton">Jack Charlton</a>, manager of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland national team</a>, who had discovered that, due to his mother's place of birth, Bruce was eligible to play for Ireland. Bruce states in his autobiography that further investigation revealed that, while his earlier appearance for England B in a <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_game" title="Exhibition game">friendly match</a> was not an issue, his appearances for the England Youth team in a <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>-sanctioned tournament prohibited him from playing for the senior team of another country.<sup id="cite_ref-SB89_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB89-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> He has subsequently claimed that he chose not to play for Ireland as it would have caused problems for his club at a time when UEFA restricted the number of foreign players that a club could have in their squad in its competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-Ireland_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ireland-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>United dominated English football in the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_in_English_football" title="1993–94 in English football">1993–94 season</a>, winning a second consecutive Premier League title and then defeating Chelsea in the <a href="/wiki/1994_FA_Cup_Final" title="1994 FA Cup Final">FA Cup final</a> to become only the fourth team, and Bruce the first English captain, to win <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">The Double</a> in the 20th century,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SB1_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB1-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_in_English_football" title="1994–95 in English football">1994–95 season</a> was a disappointing one for Bruce and United, as the club failed in its bid to win a third consecutive Premier League title and lost to Everton in the <a href="/wiki/1995_FA_Cup_Final" title="1995 FA Cup Final">FA Cup final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the following season Bruce was offered the job of manager by three clubs, but Ferguson refused to allow him to pursue the opportunities as he felt the player still had a role to play in the United team.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Bruce made a further 30&#160;Premier League appearances,<sup id="cite_ref-all_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-all-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> as United managed to overcome a 12-point deficit to Newcastle United to win the championship once again.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> A week later he was left out of United's squad for the <a href="/wiki/1996_FA_Cup_Final" title="1996 FA Cup Final">FA Cup final</a> due to a slight injury.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the match <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cantona" title="Eric Cantona">Eric Cantona</a>, who had captained the team and scored the only goal in a 1–0 win over Liverpool, attempted to persuade Bruce to be the one to receive the trophy, but Bruce declined.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Ferguson denied that Bruce's omission was a sign that his time at the club was nearing an end,<sup id="cite_ref-Leaving_MU_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leaving_MU-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> but Bruce, then 35&#160;years old, believed that he would be unlikely to be selected for the team during the year remaining on his contract.<sup id="cite_ref-Leaving_MU2_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leaving_MU2-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> He opted instead to join First Division club <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a> on a <a href="/wiki/Free_transfer_(association_football)" title="Free transfer (association football)">free transfer</a>, having signed a contract valued at nearly £2&#160;million over two years, which made him one of the highest-paid players in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Leaving_MU_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leaving_MU-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_playing_career">Later playing career</span></h3>
<p>Bruce was among five former Premier League players signed by Birmingham manager <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Francis" title="Trevor Francis">Trevor Francis</a> to add experience to a squad expected to challenge for promotion.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> He was made captain of the team,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> but his Birmingham career was dogged by a series of disagreements with Francis.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Director <a href="/wiki/David_Sullivan_(businessman)" title="David Sullivan (businessman)">David Sullivan</a> felt the need to publicly deny rumours that Bruce was lined up to replace Francis as manager after the club's stock market flotation.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> While playing for Birmingham, Bruce was the subject of several bids from his old Manchester United colleague Bryan Robson to sign for Middlesbrough, but the transfer never happened.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_in_English_football" title="1997–98 in English football">1997–98 season</a> saw Bruce dropped for the first time in his career, for a match against former club Gillingham, and he described himself as "hurt and unhappy" at being left out.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> By November 1997 he was being left out more frequently, and his omission against <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C.">Nottingham Forest</a> provoked a public war of words, which fuelled rumours that the manager was to be dismissed and that Bruce would take over as caretaker until the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the season he accepted the post of <a href="/wiki/Player-manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Player-manager">player-manager</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a>. Though the deal was delayed while Birmingham attempted to negotiate a transfer fee for his playing contract,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> he took up his new position on 2 July 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-Managers:_Steve_Bruce_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Managers:_Steve_Bruce-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> He played 11 matches for the club before retiring as a player, his final appearance being in a home match against Sunderland on 28 November 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-Games_played_by_Steve_Bruce_in_1998/1999_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Games_played_by_Steve_Bruce_in_1998/1999-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span></h2>
<p>During the early part of his career, Bruce's sometimes over-enthusiastic playing style, which he later described as "rampaging",<sup id="cite_ref-Buster2_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buster2-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> caused him disciplinary problems. He later developed into a solid and dependable all-round player, characterised as "an honest trier who made the absolute most of limited natural ability".<sup id="cite_ref-IP_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IP-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In his prime, he was particularly noted for his calm and deliberate passing of the ball, and his ability to control it under pressure, often with his chest. At the time, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Wright_(footballer,_born_1963)" title="Mark Wright (footballer, born 1963)">Mark Wright</a> of Liverpool was said to be the only other centre-back able to match Bruce's level of skill in these areas.<sup id="cite_ref-recovery_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recovery-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bruce was also known for his unusually high goalscoring rate for a centre-back, resulting from a combination of his ability to powerfully head the ball and his effectiveness in taking <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty kicks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Although lacking poise and grace,<sup id="cite_ref-IP_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IP-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> and often criticised for his lack of pace,<sup id="cite_ref-IP_88-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IP-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> his bravery and willingness to take knocks from opposition players made him the "heart" of the defence during his time with Manchester United.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> He was well known for continuing to play even when injured,<sup id="cite_ref-IP_88-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IP-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> including returning to the United team at short notice in 1992 even though he was awaiting an operation on a hernia.<sup id="cite_ref-recovery_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recovery-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> His indomitable spirit and motivational abilities were deemed vital to the United team,<sup id="cite_ref-IP_88-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IP-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> and Alex Ferguson has commented on his "determination and heart".<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Managerial_career">Managerial career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_managerial_career">Early managerial career</span></h3>
<p>In his first season as a manager, Bruce guided Sheffield United to eighth place in the First Division, nine points away from a place in the play-offs.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> He caused controversy when he attempted to take his team off the pitch during an FA Cup match against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>. Bruce felt that the Gunners had broken an unwritten rule of sportsmanship by scoring the winning goal from a throw-in instead of returning the ball to United, who had intentionally kicked it out of play to allow an injured player to be attended to. Although the game eventually continued to a finish, following a gesture by Arsenal the match was declared void and replayed.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> In May 1999, Bruce resigned from his post after just one season in charge, citing turmoil in the club's boardroom and a shortage of funds for transfers.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> He contemplated leaving football for a job in television but was persuaded by <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a> owner Barry Rubery to become the club's manager.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Huddersfield were early promotion contenders in the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_in_English_football" title="1999–2000 in English football">1999–2000 season</a>, winning six consecutive matches to rise to third place in the First Division table by late November,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> but lost form and failed to reach the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship_play-offs" title="EFL Championship play-offs">play-offs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The team continued to struggle at the start of the <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_in_English_football" title="2000–01 in English football">2000–01 season</a>, gaining just six points from 11 matches, and Bruce was sacked in October 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> He then became involved in a dispute with Rubery, who accused him of "wasting" £3m on players and having "an ego to feed".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Although he was linked with the manager's job at <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Bruce remained out of the game until he was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a> in April 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The team reached the Second Division play-offs but lost in the semi-finals,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> and Bruce almost immediately left the club, where he had been in charge for less than two months, to take over as manager of Crystal Palace.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although his new club began the <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_in_English_football" title="2001–02 in English football">2001–02 season</a> strongly, topping the First Division table and looking well placed for regaining the Premier League place that the club had last held in the 1997–98 season,<sup id="cite_ref-hurry_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurry-125">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Bruce tendered his resignation less than three months into the season in order to return to Birmingham City as manager. Although he was initially prevented from doing so by an injunction taken out by Crystal Palace, he was eventually allowed to join the Midlands-based club after a compensation package was agreed.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> By now he had acquired a reputation as a manager who rarely held down a job for a significant length of time.<sup id="cite_ref-hurry_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurry-125">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birmingham_City">Birmingham City</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steve_Bruce_pre-season_Germany_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Steve_Bruce_pre-season_Germany_2004.jpg/170px-Steve_Bruce_pre-season_Germany_2004.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Steve_Bruce_pre-season_Germany_2004.jpg/255px-Steve_Bruce_pre-season_Germany_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Steve_Bruce_pre-season_Germany_2004.jpg/340px-Steve_Bruce_pre-season_Germany_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steve_Bruce_pre-season_Germany_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bruce managing <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a> in 2004</div></div></div>
<p>Upon his arrival, the Blues were in a mid-table position in the First Division,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> but a lengthy unbeaten run saw the team qualify for the play-offs.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The team went on to beat Bruce's former club Norwich City in the final after a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-out</a> to gain promotion to the Premier League, ending a 16-year absence from the top level of English football.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Birmingham spent the early part of the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_in_English_football" title="2002–03 in English football">2002–03 season</a> struggling near the foot of the Premier League table, but Bruce's signing of <a href="/wiki/Christophe_Dugarry" title="Christophe Dugarry">Christophe Dugarry</a> revitalised the team, who ended the season in 13th place and finished higher than local rivals <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> for the first time since the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The following season began well for Birmingham, who climbed as high as fourth in the table, but the team's fortunes declined and they could only finish in tenth place at the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Despite this disappointment, Bruce signed a new contract in June 2004 designed to keep him at <a href="/wiki/St_Andrew%27s_(stadium)" title="St Andrew&#39;s (stadium)">St Andrew's</a> for a further five years,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> but just two months later <a href="/wiki/Freddy_Shepherd" title="Freddy Shepherd">Freddy Shepherd</a>, chairman of Newcastle United, was reported to have made Bruce his main target in the search for a new manager to replace Bobby Robson. The club was reportedly prepared to pay Birmingham more than £3&#160;million in compensation, and Bruce himself was said to be keen to take over at St James' Park,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> but he ultimately remained at Birmingham. He stated that "as far as I'm concerned, I've got a job to do [at Birmingham City] and I'm determined to get on with it", but it was also reported that Newcastle would have been required to pay a much larger compensation fee or face legal action had he been persuaded to switch clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Initial expectations were high for the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_in_English_football" title="2004–05 in English football">2004–05 season</a>, but the club once again finished in a mid-table position, ending the season in 12th&#160;place.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the sacking of <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Souness" title="Graeme Souness">Graeme Souness</a> as Newcastle manager in February 2006, Bruce was again linked with the job,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> which ultimately went to <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Roeder" title="Glenn Roeder">Glenn Roeder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> By this stage of the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_in_English_football" title="2005–06 in English football">2005–06 season</a>, Birmingham were struggling in the league, and on 21 March 2006 were beaten 7–0 at home by Liverpool in the FA Cup quarter-finals.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Some supporters of the club began to call for his resignation, but Bruce insisted that he would fight on as manager.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The team managed to climb out of the relegation zone for the first time in nearly six months after a win over <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> in early April 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> However, they were soon overtaken by Portsmouth, whose victory over Wigan Athletic on 29 April left Birmingham mathematically unable to match their points total and therefore relegated.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although Bruce had the largest transfer budget in the division made available to him,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Birmingham made a slow start to the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_in_English_football" title="2006–07 in English football">2006–07 season</a> in the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a> and, after a 1–0 defeat at home to Norwich City, the team's fifth consecutive match without a win, there were calls from fans and local journalists for the manager to be sacked.<sup id="cite_ref-Gold_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gold-144">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gold2_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gold2-145">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Bruce publicly accepted responsibility for the team's poor run and admitted that he feared for his job,<sup id="cite_ref-Fear_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fear-146">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> but the team responded with a 1–0 victory over Derby County,<sup id="cite_ref-chant_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chant-147">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> and then recorded a further five consecutive league victories to be joint leaders of the league table by late November.<sup id="cite_ref-top_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-148">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> On 29 April 2007, Birmingham secured promotion to the Premier League, with one match to play, by virtue of Derby County's 2–0 defeat at Crystal Palace. Chairman <a href="/wiki/David_Gold_(businessman)" title="David Gold (businessman)">David Gold</a> told the press "There have been some dark days but Steve has been outstanding. He was determined to bounce back. He has rebuilt the team and now we are all back where we want to be."<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wigan_Athletic">Wigan Athletic</span></h3>
<p>In May 2007, Birmingham's board agreed a new contract for Bruce, but the unwillingness of the club's prospective purchaser <a href="/wiki/Carson_Yeung" title="Carson Yeung">Carson Yeung</a> to ratify it left his future uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> In October 2007, Bolton Wanderers were refused permission to speak to him about their managerial vacancy.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
Later that month, Bruce and Yeung held a meeting which reportedly had positive results.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Bruce later claimed that Birmingham's managing director <a href="/wiki/Karren_Brady" title="Karren Brady">Karren Brady</a> had "shafted" him on a new contract with the club,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> and when Wigan Athletic requested permission to speak to Bruce about their managerial vacancy, he was receptive to their approach.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> As required under the terms of his contract, Wigan agreed to pay Birmingham a then-<a href="/wiki/Transfer_(association_football)#Managers" title="Transfer (association football)">world record</a> compensation for the loss of his services of around £3m,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> and they were then allowed to speak to him. On 19 November, Wigan announced the signing of Bruce for a second time.<sup id="cite_ref-left_Birmingham_BBC_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-left_Birmingham_BBC-157">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 November, during a press conference which was intended to formally present Bruce as the new manager of Wigan, the club's chief executive Brenda Spencer informed the media that the deal had been put on hold by "unknown issues" between Bruce and Birmingham City, reported to centre on the advance payment of the image rights element of Bruce's contract at St Andrew's.<sup id="cite_ref-left_Birmingham_BBC2_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-left_Birmingham_BBC2-158">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-imagerights_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imagerights-159">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> On 23 November 2007 Wigan announced that Bruce had now signed his contract and would officially rejoin the Latics.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCconfirmWigan_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCconfirmWigan-160">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> His first game in charge was a 1–1 home draw with <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> on 1 December 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-firstgameback_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-firstgameback-161">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Wigan spent the remainder of the season struggling against relegation, but the club secured Premier League survival with victory over Aston Villa in the penultimate game of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCWigan_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCWigan-162">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> In September 2008, Bruce was once again linked with the manager's job at Newcastle United following the departure of <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Keegan" title="Kevin Keegan">Kevin Keegan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LEP_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LEP-164">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bruce led Wigan to an 11th-place finish in the 2008–09 season,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> despite the loss of midfielder <a href="/wiki/Wilson_Palacios" title="Wilson Palacios">Wilson Palacios</a> to Tottenham Hotspur in the January transfer window.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sunderland">Sunderland</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mikel_Arteta_2_(6270706966).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Mikel_Arteta_2_%286270706966%29.jpg/220px-Mikel_Arteta_2_%286270706966%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Mikel_Arteta_2_%286270706966%29.jpg/330px-Mikel_Arteta_2_%286270706966%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Mikel_Arteta_2_%286270706966%29.jpg/440px-Mikel_Arteta_2_%286270706966%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mikel_Arteta_2_(6270706966).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bruce managing <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>On 27 May 2009, Bruce was reported to have been given permission to talk to Sunderland about succeeding <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Sbragia" title="Ricky Sbragia">Ricky Sbragia</a>, who resigned as manager after the last match of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Bruce was confirmed as the new manager of Sunderland on 3 June after signing a three-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> He was joined at Sunderland by three of his former Wigan Athletic coaching staff, assistant <a href="/wiki/Eric_Black" title="Eric Black">Eric Black</a>, goalkeeping coach <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Spink" title="Nigel Spink">Nigel Spink</a>, and reserve team coach <a href="/wiki/Keith_Bertschin" title="Keith Bertschin">Keith Bertschin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> In his first season at Sunderland, despite a run of 14 games without a win, Bruce led the Black Cats to a 13th-place finish in the Premier League.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bruce made wholesale changes to Sunderland's squad, signing 13 players and selling 15 in his first 18 months at the club.<sup id="cite_ref-taylor_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taylor-171">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> On 25 February 2011, Bruce signed an extension to his contract, keeping him at Sunderland until 2014, with chairman <a href="/wiki/Niall_Quinn" title="Niall Quinn">Niall Quinn</a> stating that "In only 18 months he has reshaped our squad beyond recognition, bringing in some fantastically talented players. He embodies the ethos of teamwork and the importance of camaraderie in creating a wonderful spirit of togetherness amongst the players and staff".<sup id="cite_ref-taylor_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taylor-171">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bruce was dismissed as manager on 30 November 2011, with Sunderland in 16th position following a poor run of form which culminated with a 2–1 home defeat to bottom club Wigan four days earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> He later linked his dismissal from the managerial post with the fact that he is a fan of Newcastle United, Sunderland's <a href="/wiki/Tyne%E2%80%93Wear_derby" title="Tyne–Wear derby">bitter rivals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hull_City">Hull City</span></h3>
<p>On 8 June 2012, Bruce was appointed as manager at Championship club <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a> on a three-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-Steve_Bruce_appointed_Hull_City_manager_on_three-year_deal_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steve_Bruce_appointed_Hull_City_manager_on_three-year_deal-174">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> In his first season with the club, he led them to promotion to the Premier League, clinching second place in the Championship on the final day of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The following season, the "Tigers" came 16th with a club record tally of 37 points,<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> and reached the final of the FA Cup for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> They took a two-goal lead in the first ten minutes of <a href="/wiki/2014_FA_Cup_Final" title="2014 FA Cup Final">the final</a>, but opponents Arsenal scored a goal in each half to take the game into extra-time and then scored a third to win the trophy.<sup id="cite_ref-Arsenal_3-2_Hull_City_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arsenal_3-2_Hull_City-178">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Reaching the final qualified Hull for the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2014–15 UEFA Europa League">2014–15 UEFA Europa League</a>, their first European campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2015, Bruce signed a three-year contract extension.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> A run of poor form left Hull near the bottom of the table going into the final game of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_in_English_football" title="2014–15 in English football">2014–15</a> season and needing to defeat Bruce's former club Manchester United to stand any chance of avoiding relegation.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> They could only manage a 0–0 draw and were relegated to the Championship. The poor performances of a number of players signed by Bruce, including club record signing <a href="/wiki/Abel_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Abel Hernández">Abel Hernández</a>, were identified as key factors in the club's failure to remain in the Premier League.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2016, Bruce won the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship_Manager_of_the_Month" title="EFL Championship Manager of the Month">Championship Manager of the Month</a> after leading Hull to four victories; Hernández, who scored six times, got the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship_Player_of_the_Month" title="EFL Championship Player of the Month">players' equivalent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hull&#39;s_Steve_Bruce_and_Abel_Hernandez_land_January&#39;s_Sky_Bet_Championship_awards_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hull&#39;s_Steve_Bruce_and_Abel_Hernandez_land_January&#39;s_Sky_Bet_Championship_awards-183">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Hull finished the season in fourth, qualifying for <a href="/wiki/2016_Football_League_play-offs" title="2016 Football League play-offs">the play-offs</a>, where they defeated Derby County in the semi-finals. In the final on 28 May, a 25-yard goal from <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Diam%C3%A9" title="Mohamed Diamé">Mohamed Diamé</a> against Sheffield Wednesday won Hull promotion to the Premier League for the second time during Bruce's spell in charge. Bruce said after the game that he had considered resignation following the team's relegation, and would hold talks with the prospective new owners to be assured of his future.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> In July 2016, with his future at Hull seemingly still uncertain, he was interviewed by officials of <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">The Football Association</a> concerning the vacant position of manager of England.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, Bruce met with Hull City officials and announced his resignation later that day<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> amid claims he became frustrated by a lack of transfer activity at the club.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aston_Villa">Aston Villa</span></h3>
<p>On 12 October 2016, Bruce was appointed manager of Championship club Aston Villa.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> In his second match in charge, Villa defeated <a href="/wiki/Reading_F.C." title="Reading F.C.">Reading</a>, the club's first win in 11 games and the first away win for 14 months.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> He brought in <a href="/wiki/Colin_Calderwood" title="Colin Calderwood">Colin Calderwood</a> as assistant manager from <a href="/wiki/Brighton_%26_Hove_Albion" class="mw-redirect" title="Brighton &amp; Hove Albion">Brighton &amp; Hove Albion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Clemence" title="Stephen Clemence">Stephen Clemence</a> from old club Hull City as first-team coach.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_in_English_football" title="2017–18 in English football">2017–18</a> season, Villa secured a play-off place and defeated Middlesbrough to reach <a href="/wiki/2018_EFL_Championship_play-off_Final" title="2018 EFL Championship play-off Final">the final</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> but lost 1–0 to <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a> in the final and thus missed out on promotion to the Premier League.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> On 2 October 2018, Villa surrendered a two-goal lead, drawing 3–3 at home to bottom club <a href="/wiki/Preston_North_End_F.C." title="Preston North End F.C.">Preston North End</a>.  One spectator threw a cabbage at Bruce and there were calls from home fans on the <a href="/wiki/Holte_End" class="mw-redirect" title="Holte End">Holte End</a> for Bruce to go.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The following day, he was sacked by Villa after a poor run of form.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sheffield_Wednesday">Sheffield Wednesday</span></h3>
<p>In January 2019, Bruce was appointed manager of Championship club <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a> with effect from the start of the following month.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> On 27 January, his delay in taking up this appointment was criticised by <i><a href="/wiki/Match_of_the_Day" title="Match of the Day">Match of the Day</a></i> pundits  <a href="/wiki/Danny_Murphy_(footballer,_born_1977)" title="Danny Murphy (footballer, born 1977)">Danny Murphy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Gullit" title="Ruud Gullit">Ruud Gullit</a> during a 3–0 FA Cup defeat away to Chelsea.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Bruce subsequently defended his decision, as he had had two operations since leaving Aston Villa and needed time to recuperate, as well as the need to recover from the death of both his parents in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newcastle_United">Newcastle United</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">BBC Sport</a> reported in July 2019 that Bruce had resigned from his position at Wednesday,<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> after he earlier admitted that he had held talks with Premier League <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> over their managerial vacancy.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>  His appointment at Newcastle was confirmed on 17 July. <sup id="cite_ref-newcastle-appoint_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newcastle-appoint-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Sheffield Wednesday, however, soon filed a report to the Premier League alleging misconduct in his appointment,<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> stating that there were still outstanding legal issues with Bruce having resigned just 48 hours earlier, whilst also suspecting that confidential details of Bruce's contract were leaked making it impossible for him to remain at the club.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Newcastle United denied any wrongdoing and stated that they were confident no case could be escalated.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Reaction from the fans was mixed, with some feeling Bruce would not achieve the standard set by predecessor <a href="/wiki/Rafa_Ben%C3%ADtez" class="mw-redirect" title="Rafa Benítez">Rafa Benítez</a>, whilst his recent lack of Premier League football and management of rival club Sunderland proved controversial.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Bruce acknowledged Benítez's popularity and stated he hoped the fans would not rush to judgement and give him time to prove himself.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Due to <a href="/wiki/Visa_policy_of_China" title="Visa policy of China">visa problems in China</a>, Bruce watched his first match as manager from the stands which saw Newcastle achieve a third-place finish in the pre-season <a href="/wiki/2019_Premier_League_Asia_Trophy" title="2019 Premier League Asia Trophy">2019 Premier League Asia Trophy</a> following a 1-0 victory over <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Shanghai_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shanghai-208">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Bruce soon made six signings,<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> notably securing <a href="/wiki/Joelinton_Cassio_Apolin%C3%A1rio_de_Lira" class="mw-redirect" title="Joelinton Cassio Apolinário de Lira">Joelinton</a> from <a href="/wiki/TSG_1899_Hoffenheim" title="TSG 1899 Hoffenheim">TSG 1899 Hoffenheim</a> for £40 million, breaking the club's transfer fee record previously set by the purchase of <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Almir%C3%B3n" title="Miguel Almirón">Miguel Almirón</a> for £21 million six months earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_outside_football">Life outside football</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h3>
<p>Bruce has been married since February 1983 to Janet (née Smith),<sup id="cite_ref-express_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-express-220">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-irish_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irish-221">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> who is also from the <a href="/wiki/Hexham" title="Hexham">Hexham</a> area, and went to the same school as Bruce.<sup id="cite_ref-SB38_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SB38-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The couple have two children, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Bruce_(footballer,_born_1984)" title="Alex Bruce (footballer, born 1984)">Alex</a> (born 1984) and Amy (born 1987).<sup id="cite_ref-express_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-express-220">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> Alex is also a footballer, and was signed by his father for Hull City in July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> He had previously played under his father's management at Birmingham City, but left the club in 2006, in part due to accusations of <a href="/wiki/Nepotism" title="Nepotism">nepotism</a> levelled at his father.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Amy was linked romantically with Aston Villa player <a href="/wiki/Lee_Hendrie" title="Lee Hendrie">Lee Hendrie</a> in tabloid newspaper stories in 2004, which provoked an angry response from her father, who described the reports as "lies", and claimed that journalists had gone so far as to contact his doctor and examine his household waste in an attempt to uncover gossip.<sup id="cite_ref-Lee2_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lee2-225">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> In September 2004, Bruce was involved in an altercation outside his home with two men who were attempting to steal his daughter's car. The affray left him with facial injuries but did not prevent him from travelling to a Premier League match the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-bruise_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bruise-226">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> After the incident one newspaper attempted to connect it with the allegations concerning Hendrie, leading Bruce to contemplate legal action.<sup id="cite_ref-Lee2_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lee2-225">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_activities">Other activities</span></h3>
<p>Bruce's autobiography, <i>Heading for Victory</i>, was published in 1994. In 1999, while manager of Huddersfield, he wrote a trio of novels:  <i>Striker!</i>, <i>Sweeper!</i> and <i>Defender!</i>. The books centred on fictional football manager Steve Barnes, based on Bruce, who solved murder mysteries and thwarted terrorists. Bruce later expressed his embarrassment at the books, which have become sought-after collectables.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
